Municipal Chamber of Commerce 155

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the National Government in Nanjing: The political expenses of the government are insufficient, and there is a proposal to suspend the payment of principal and interest on various domestic debts. We are deeply shocked to hear of this measure of drinking poison to quench thirst. Since the National Government's Northern Expedition and unification, domestic debts have been issued over the years to fill political expenses, amounting to no less than 700 to 800 million. If voluntary subscriptions are not enough, compulsory distribution is followed. The people do not have such large amounts of spare funds, but they force themselves to subscribe because it is related to maintaining the party and the country. All the people's hard-earned money has been poured into government bonds. Fortunately, the repayment of principal and interest has been able to maintain credit, so the people treat the bonds they hold the same as field deeds and house contracts, relying on them for their annual savings. Moreover, since bandits and communists have spread everywhere in recent years, people in various provinces who own real estate have been divided and seized. They have no choice but to gather their cash in cities and exchange it for bonds to make a living. Now, if the payment of principal and interest is suspended, all the bonds will be turned into waste paper. It is as if the government has announced the confiscation of the people's property. The people have done their best to protect the party and the country and bought these bonds, but today they get this result. If the people go bankrupt, the government will not be able to survive. In today's situation where sincere cooperation has just been unified, the government should not rectify its discipline to stop the interception of tax revenue and strictly eliminate redundant troops and wasteful expenses. Instead, it abandons the credibility of the government and plunders the sources of the people's livelihood. We are afraid that the people will suspect each other and think that the government's stability is just a manifestation of bullying the few and fearing the strong. Even if the principal and interest are suspended, it will only inspire the ambition of tax interceptors and help the extravagant. How much benefit will it bring to the government's finances? It will only make the commerce and finance bankrupt and follow in the footsteps of Soviet Russia and Germany after the war. The strength of recovery cannot be compared with Russia and Germany. Then our country will truly fall into a state of irrecoverability. What is called danger cannot be ignored. We painfully express our sincere opinions. We humbly request that you, the members of the government, keep in mind that this matter is of great importance and do not make such a bad move. Save a ray of hope for the country. We would be very grateful. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully kowtows.

Wang Xiaolai, a member of the 2.5% Treasury Bond Custody Committee, made a statement yesterday: Today, there is a widespread rumor in the city that the government will suspend the payment of principal and interest on domestic bonds. All sectors of the city are extremely panic-stricken. All the public bonds and treasury bonds issued repeatedly are guaranteed by national credit. Now, if the principal and interest are suspended, how will we show our great trust? Looking at the financial community across the country, bonds are used as a guarantee for issuing banknotes. If the principal and interest are not paid, the banknotes will also be affected, and the national finance will be in a state of stagnation. How can the country survive? This is not only related to the protection of the sources of livelihood for social organizations, common people, orphans, and widows, but also to the foundation of the country. Therefore, we will do our best to consolidate it at any cost.

Northwest Test Flight Completed 156

Li Jingcong and Others Arrived in Shanghai on Aircraft No. 1 Yesterday

Li Discusses the Circumstances of the Northwest Test Flight

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation previously sent Aircraft Navigation Team Leader Smith, Operations Team Leader Li Jingcong, and pilot Luzi to the Northwest to prepare for a test flight. They have successfully returned. Li and Smith arrived in Beijing from Ping on the 12th and arrived in Shanghai from Beijing at 3:00 PM yesterday, landing at Hongqiao Airport in this city at 4:35 PM. This test flight was longer than that of Lin Bai Ke and could break the Far East aviation record. All employees of the Eurasia Corporation went to the airport to welcome them. The details are recorded below.

Welcoming Personnel: Yesterday morning, the company received a telegram from Mr. Li in Tokyo, saying that he would take a flight from Beijing to Shanghai at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. After receiving the telegram, the company led all employees to the station to welcome them at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, including Vice Chairman Shuang Qing, German Director Von Sicke, Chinese Director and Director of the Postal Remittance and Savings Bureau Liu Fan, Director of the Postal Bureau Qian Chunqi, Director of the Finance Team Wang Zihan, Secretaries Sun Mutang and Shen Yani, and directors and employees of the Shanghai Station.

Arrival in Shanghai: At 4:35 PM in the afternoon, everyone saw Eurasia Aircraft No. 1 approaching from afar, as small as a dragonfly flying in the clouds and tumbling in the sky. They raised flags and hats to welcome it. Before long, Aircraft No. 1 flew to Hongqiao Airport, circled several times, and landed. There were five people in the aircraft, namely Operations Team Leader Li Jingcong, Aircraft Navigation Team Leader Smith, German Lufthansa representative Huier Tuo, pilot Luzi, and the pilot's assistant. After Li and others got out of the aircraft, they shook hands with the people in the company and were very happy. Miss Shouyong, the daughter of Shuang Qing, presented bouquets of flowers to everyone to celebrate the success of the test flight.

The Success of the Northwest Test Flight (Photo Taken by This Newspaper) 157

From right to left: Miss Shuang Shouyong, Mr. Shuang Qing, Mr. Luzi, Mr. Li Jingcong, Mr. Smith, and a telegraph operator.

Li's Remarks: A reporter from the New Voice News Agency went to Hongqiao Airport yesterday to meet with Mr. Li Jingcong and asked about the course of the test flight in the Northwest. According to him, it was quite detailed and contained many treasures. Li said, "The distance from Beiping to Dihua is more than 4,400 kilometers, which is about 8,000 li in Chinese. We took off from Ping at 7:00 AM on the 22nd of last month, reached Guihua at 10:00 AM, stopped briefly, refueled, and flew again. We arrived at the Ruoshui River at 4:00 PM in the afternoon and stopped in the ancient city. On the morning of the 21st, we flew the plane again. We landed and refueled at the oil storage location at noon, and then stayed in the Ruoshui River. On the morning of the 22nd, we flew to Dihua and arrived there at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. The chairman of Xinjiang Province, Jin Shuren, led personnel from various agencies to welcome us because it was the first time a flight had arrived there.

A Glimpse of the Ancient City: The reporter also asked about the situation in the Northwest and the scenery of the ancient city. According to Li, the so-called ancient city is next to the Ruoshui River, in front of Heichengzi. The city walls have been buried in the soil and are not easy to identify. Only vaguely, the shape of broken tiles and ruined walls is revealed. The area of the city is about one mile in circumference and was built in the Han Dynasty, reaching more than 2,000 years. There are no people or animals in the city, and there are no aquatic plants or houses. The ground is full of desert and boundless. During the day, the world changes color, and the weather is abnormal.

General Situation in the Northwest: Li also talked about the situation in the Northwest, saying that the weather in the Northwest is very cold. There are heating appliances on the plane during the test flight, and it is even colder at night. The words of the ancients that the Hu land is frozen and the frontier soldiers are miserable can be seen today. At night, the beasts howl. Among these four thousand four hundred kilometers from Ping to Dihua, there are either high mountains or deserts. There are very few rivers. From Baotou to Hami, the border of Xinjiang, there are more than one thousand kilometers, all of which are deserts and there are few traces of people. The rest of the places are also very desolate. Dihua is the capital of Xinjiang Province, but it is not very lively. The more prosperous one is Dachen, which is located in the south of the Tianshan Mountains. There are very few Han Chinese living in the Northwest, and most of them are ethnic groups. There are also many Turkish and Indian merchants.

Formal Flight: The success of this Northwest test flight of the company was unexpected. Before the event, British and German people speculated that it would not be easy to succeed. The company is very pleased with this achievement. It has now ordered four aircraft from Germany to prepare for formal flights. The opening date has not yet been determined and must be decided by the board of directors. It will probably be realized in March of this spring. After that, a flight from Shanghai to Dihua, Xinjiang, will only take two or three days to arrive, which is a world of difference from the previous road travel.

Bringing Back Mail: It is said that the people in the post office said that the Eurasia Aviation Corporation sent Eurasia Aircraft No. 1 to test fly the new route from Beiping to Xinjiang. After arriving safely in Dihua, it started its return journey on the 7th and brought back a small amount of mail. The mail was sent from Dihua Post Office on January 7, and the part sent to Shanghai was transferred to Shanghai by the Beijing-Shanghai night train last night (the 12th). It took only six days on the way, and its speed of transfer created a new record in the history of Chinese transportation.

Another Case of Counterfeit Cotton Yarn Cracked 169

Dafeng Cotton Yarn Shop in the French Concession

Forty-Three Bales of Japanese Yarn Seized

Recently, Japanese cotton yarn has been found in the market masquerading as domestic Shenxin Yarn Factory products. After the Shenxin Yarn Factory cracked the case and handed over the suspects and evidence to the First Special District Court for interrogation, the details have been reported in the newspapers. Now, it has been reported that Zheng Kang, the owner of the Dafeng Cotton Yarn Shop at No. 50 Xixin Bridge, French Concession, recently altered the packaging of 42 bales of Japanese Blue Wind brand cotton yarn to masquerade as Shenxin Yarn Factory's products and sell them on the market. After the Shenxin Factory learned of this, it reported the matter to the Public Concession Police, which then requested the French Police to send detective Gu Mingzhou to the Dafeng Yarn Shop to seize 43 bales of counterfeit cotton yarn, along with the shop owner Zheng Kang, and bring them to the police station. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, they were handed over to the First Division of the Second Special Court. Judge Ma Shounan ascended the bench to interrogate them. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the case, saying that the defendant sold Japanese goods as domestic goods and is now being prosecuted under Article 269 of the Criminal Code for hindering agriculture, industry, and commerce, and requested a continuance for investigation and verification. The plaintiff, Shenxin Yarn Factory, represented by employee Tong Jiarui, filed a complaint, requesting that the law be strictly enforced. When questioned, Zheng Kang confessed that he was a merchant and that the 16-count Ren Zhong brand was indeed affixed to the Blue Wind brand yarn. He stated that he had purchased this cotton yarn three or four months ago and did not dare to counterfeit it. When asked where he purchased it, he replied that he did not remember clearly and hired lawyer Gu Jirong to defend him, requesting that the defendant be allowed to post bail pending the adjourned hearing. The police lawyer objected, and the court did not allow bail. Judge Ma Shounan announced that the hearing would be adjourned to the morning of the 20th and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Workers of Tongxing Factory Beaten 170

Workers of the Japanese-owned Tongxing Yarn Factory at No. 181 Gordon Road, previously angered by the factory's dismissal of a large number of workers, arbitrary oppression, increased workload, and deduction of wages, conspired to deal with the situation. The factory had been preventing workers from entering the factory since the 9th. The workers sent ten representatives to negotiate with the factory at around 2 p.m. yesterday. At that time, about 200 to 300 workers gathered outside the door while waiting for news. The Pudu Road Police, responsible for maintaining order, dispatched many detectives to patrol nearby. However, police officers No. 1 and No. 45 suddenly ordered the workers to disperse and drove them away for some reason, resulting in a conflict between the two sides. As a result, three workers were beaten and injured, and the Japanese police chief was also injured in the head. The workers then dispersed, and the injured workers were sent to the hospital by the police while investigating the cause of the incident for further action.

Commemorative Stamps for Martyrs Expected to Be Issued in Early February 171

The Beijing Printing Bureau is Rushing to Print Them

Not Yet Available for Sale in Beijing and Shanghai on New Year's Day

The Directorate General of Posts of the whole country previously instructed the Ministry of Communications to order the postal districts of all provinces to issue commemorative stamps for martyrs on January 1. The Directorate General of Posts also planned to first issue them in Beijing and Shanghai if the Beijing Printing Bureau, which was responsible for printing the stamps, did not send many stamps by the deadline. However, because the printed stamps have not yet been shipped to Shanghai, they have not yet been issued. According to a letter from the Beijing Bureau, the martyr stamps are currently being printed urgently, and a batch of printed stamps is scheduled to arrive in early February this year (around the end of the lunar year). If the quantity is not sufficient, they will still be issued first in Beijing and Shanghai.

Mortality Rate in the Concessions 174

Slight Increase Last Month

Smallpox is Quite Prevalent

According to a report from the Health Department of the Public Concession, in December of last year, 59 foreigners died inside and outside the concession, accounting for 18.66 per thousand. 1,494 Chinese died, accounting for 18.2 per thousand. Compared with the usual situation, the mortality rate of the Chinese has slightly increased.

Smallpox was quite prevalent last month. It is estimated that 22 foreigners contracted the disease, with 8 deaths. It is estimated that 46 Chinese reported to have contracted the disease, with 30 deaths. As a result, the Health Department is quite anxious about this. It is estimated that during this month, the department's revaccination team vaccinated a total of 6,657 people, and the various health sub-bureaus vaccinated a total of 4,067 people. All Chinese and Indian patrol officers were vaccinated this month. The number of vaccinations by the patrol team is less than before because most factories and schools have already completed vaccinations, and the timing of this month is also not favored by the Chinese.

The Health Department's rescue team will be merged into the Fire Department's rescue team. The procedures have now been completed. After the two teams are merged, not only can expenses be saved, but also the duplication of agencies in the same bureau can be avoided, so that the public does not know where to turn. From now on, all emergency incidents, whether due to fire, illness, or other accidents, will be handled by the Fire Department's rescue team.

City Public Works Bureau's Collection of Vehicle License Stamp Tax: The Process 178

A letter from the City Public Works Bureau states: "Our bureau is currently re-issuing vehicle licenses for the 21st year. For automobiles, horse-drawn carriages, and privately owned pedicabs, we are collecting stamp tax on each license. Outsiders are unaware of the truth and are vying to inquire. The stamp tax payable on vehicle licenses is stipulated in the central government's Stamp Tax Regulations, and our bureau's collection is simply fulfilling the obligations of the licensing authority. To provide an answer, we are publishing a summary of the process: The matter of affixing stamps to vehicle licenses in this city began in December of the 16th year. At that time, our bureau had just completed the registration, inspection, and issuance of licenses for various vehicles in the city. On December 1st, the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Baoshan County and Shanghai Zhabei District branch sent a letter to our bureau, requesting us to affix stamps on behalf of vehicle owners when they renew their licenses, and promised to pay a handling fee. On December 12th of the same month, the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Shanghai South District branch also made the same request. In June of the following year and in the month of the 19th year, the Jiangsu Shangbao and Special District Stamp Tax Bureau again sent letters requesting assistance. Because our bureau considered that the vehicle licenses in this city were donation licenses, which were different from those elsewhere, we did not respond. This is the past. In the first half of last year, according to reports from Youhua Automobile Company and Tongshunji Automobile Transportation Company, the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau detained licenses and vehicles, and arbitrarily imposed fines, causing a lot of disputes and damaging business. After discussions with the Finance and Public Security Bureaus, it was also agreed that the vehicle licenses in this city were donation certificates, and the various vehicle licenses listed in the Stamp Tax Regulations, detailed in Article 1, are intended to refer to personal certificates. The two are of different nature. Affixing stamps to donation licenses would be a form of double taxation. We immediately submitted a report to the Municipal Government, requesting the Ministry of Finance to allow the various vehicle licenses in this city to be exempt from stamps to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. Later, we received a response from the ministry stating, 'Liquor business licenses are also certificates issued by the government for collecting business tax. Over the years, all provinces have complied with the regulations and affixed stamps, which is largely the same as the situation with automobile licenses. There is no double taxation involved. The request for exemption involves changing the regulations and cannot be approved.' Later, the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau sent representatives to discuss methods for exempting the stamp tax on vehicle licenses or adding a stamp. Our bureau proposed that large freight vehicles (i.e., hand-pulled carts) and bicycles (mostly used by workers or lower-level employees of government agencies for transportation, hoping to reduce daily transportation costs) should be exempt to show consideration. The Stamp Tax Bureau also agreed. As a result, the Stamp Tax Bureau issued a notice, and our bureau began collecting the tax on behalf of the government when re-issuing vehicle licenses for the 21st year from December 25th of the 20th year. Regarding the tax collected by our bureau, the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau, following the precedent of assisting in the promotion of stamp sales, sent a letter instructing us to retain 5% of the handling fee and remit it monthly at 50% of the actual amount. On December 12th of the 20th year, we reported this to the Municipal Government, stating that the handling fee would be fully reported and remitted to the municipal treasury at any time. We then received Directive No. 13046, approving the record. This is the beginning and end of our bureau's collection of stamp tax on vehicle licenses. In summary, our bureau's attitude towards this case and the purpose of our handling are as follows: ㈠ Our bureau initially did not recognize the affixing of stamps to vehicle licenses, so the matter of vehicle license stamps in this city was suspended from the end of the 16th year to the beginning of the 20th year, for a total of four years. ㈡ Our bureau has full responsibility for the management of vehicles in the city. Since the Ministry of Finance could not exempt vehicle licenses from stamps, and the method for affixing stamps to vehicle licenses should be handled by the licensing authority, it is better for our bureau to collect the tax on behalf of the government when issuing licenses to avoid disputes, rather than having the tax bureau directly inspect, reject, and fine. ㈢ Our bureau has made every effort to advocate for exemptions for all vehicle license stamps that can be exempted. The exemption for large freight vehicles and bicycles is an example. ㈣ Regarding the 5% handling fee for collecting stamp tax on vehicle licenses, the original letter from the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau stated that it would be used to 'cover the public expenses of office personnel.' However, our bureau believes that this is a handling fee paid by one government agency to another, so we declared to the Municipal Government that we would 'fully report and remit it to the municipal treasury.'"

Anti-Japanese Association's Search of Daqing Cloth Shop Case 179

Ge Yun and Others Appeal with the Police Department

Debate Postponed, Re-examination Scheduled

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association discovered that Daqing Cloth Shop, a branch opened by Deng Zhonghe at No. 1, Lane 239, Boru Road, was selling "Ten Perfection" brand cloth, which was actually Japanese "Water Moon" brand cloth that had been repackaged. On November 22nd of last year, at 10:00 a.m., the association ordered special inspection team members Ge Yunting, team leader Yang Haichang, inspectors Shi Xinmin and Ju Zongyan to lead four laborers and hire a truck to go to Daqing Shop. They confiscated eleven large packages of "Ten Perfection" brand cloth, valued at 1,760 silver taels. The shop's staff seized the opportunity to report to the Old Gate Police Station, which sent officers to arrest Ge and the other four, and handed them over to the First Special District Court for prosecution on charges of robbery under Article 348 of the Criminal Code. The presiding judge ruled that the charge of robbery could not be sustained and sentenced Ge and the other four to a fine of 20 yuan each for the crime of obstructing freedom under Article 318 of the Criminal Code, with a two-year suspended sentence. However, the police department and Ge and the others were not satisfied and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court. Yesterday afternoon, the appeal was heard. At 2:00 p.m., the criminal division chief Song Yuan, along with judges Du and Gao, took their seats in the First Criminal Court to hear the case. The police department was represented by lawyer Ru Baoyi, and Ge and the other four were defended by lawyers Chen Tingrui and Yu Hualong. Lawyer Ru began by stating, "Before presenting the grounds for the appeal, my firm would like to state the facts of the case. On November 18th of last year, eight people went to Daqing Shop, took four account books, two packages of cloth, and apprentice Zhang Haiqing onto a truck, and drove them to the Anti-Japanese Association, where they were detained for several hours. Later, his father provided a guarantor for his release, but the guarantee stated that Deng Zhonghe must be handed over within three days, otherwise the guarantor would be held responsible." At this point, lawyer Chen Tingrui objected and requested that the statement be prohibited, saying that what lawyer Ru was saying was irrelevant to the case. Lawyer Ru replied that the matter was causally related to the case and therefore needed to be stated. Judge Song ruled that it could be stated, and Lawyer Ru continued, "On the 22nd, Ge Yunting and the others went to Daqing again and took all of the 'Ten Perfection' brand cloth away. The shop's staff, Li Jiapu, reported to the police, who arrested the defendants and prosecuted them for robbery in the Special Court. At that time, Xu Fangcai, a representative from the Wusong Ten Perfection Factory, came to court to testify that the cloth taken away was produced by their factory and was indeed domestic goods. The original trial did not prosecute for robbery but imposed a fine for obstruction. However, on the night of the day the verdict was issued, Xu Fangcai, who testified in court, was suddenly arrested by more than 40 people, and the Ten Perfection Factory was sealed off. The goods were also taken away. Xu was detained for several days before being released and is now afraid to come to Shanghai and is hiding in Ningbo. The above are all facts. There are only two grounds for appeal: ㈠ Please overturn the inappropriate original judgment and sentence the appellees for the crime of robbery under Article 348; ㈡ The original trial did not mention how the stolen goods were disposed of, which is a serious oversight. Please order that they be returned to Deng Zhonghe." Judge Song then questioned Ge Yunting and the others about the grounds for the appeal. They replied, "We were executing an order from the Standing Committee and were acting purely out of patriotism. We are not satisfied with the original judgment of guilt and are appealing to have the original judgment overturned and declared innocent." He asked, "Where are the goods now?" The answer was, "In the Zhabei storage warehouse." They also said that the Ten Perfection Factory could originally only produce ten bolts of cloth per day, but after the boycott of Japanese goods, without adding any machinery, it could produce 30 bolts per day. After investigation, it was found that the cloth was produced by the Gongda Yarn Factory and rebranded as "Ten Perfection." That is why they went to seize the goods. Then, Deng Zhonghe turned himself in and testified that the cloth was indeed entirely domestic goods. If it could be proven that it was Japanese goods, he and the Ten Perfection Factory were willing to accept any punishment. The appellee's lawyer Chen said that the police department's grounds for appeal were lengthy and had just been handed down in court, so he could not adequately prepare a defense and requested that the court reschedule the hearing. Judge Song granted the request and ordered that the case be heard again at a later date.

Sheng Yulin Accused of Embezzling Large Sums 180

Formerly manager of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, now residing at No. 234, Xinxing Lane, Chongming Road, Hongkou, Changzhou native Sheng Yulin, has recently been sued in the First Special District Court by former Sanxin Yarn Factory employees Yu Hesheng, Chen Zhuting, Yu Guoxiang, and others, accusing him of embezzling large sums of money and destroying account books. The reasons for their lawsuit are as follows: In April of the 20th year, when the Sanxin Yarn Factory was sold, the factory owner ordered the defendant to sell all the scrap iron and old materials in the factory, and distribute the proceeds fairly to all colleagues in the factory. However, the defendant did not make the sale procedure public and the allocation of funds was unclear, and much of the money was embezzled. All employees publicly elected Zhu Jiyu and Cai Xin as representatives to request the publication of accounts. The defendant initially refused to hand over the accounts on the grounds that they had no right to request them. Then, they publicly elected the plaintiffs as representatives to petition the Social Affairs Bureau to order the defendant to hand over the account books. The bureau entrusted Guangde Accountants to review the accounts, and it was found that the amounts were inconsistent and that the account books had been destroyed and pages were missing. Other evidence further proves that the defendant's embezzlement is highly suspected. Therefore, the factory employees specially entrusted the plaintiffs to file a lawsuit. The case was heard last month, and both parties were summoned to court. After the plaintiffs stated the reasons for the lawsuit, Sheng Yulin claimed that he had sold the scrap materials this spring and entrusted Sun Hechai to handle the matter. All accounts were recorded by Sun, and Sun also submitted the account books to the Social Affairs Bureau. He himself had never reviewed them. Because Sun Hechai was an important witness in the case, the hearing was postponed until yesterday to summon Sun to court for further questioning. However, the summons could not be delivered, so he was still not present. The plaintiffs submitted an additional statement of reasons, stating that the sale of scrap materials at the Sanxin Factory always followed a bidding system, and the release of goods from the factory always required gate passes with detailed descriptions of the goods. However, the defendant colluded with brokers and privately exchanged goods, and gate passes were filled out by private individuals who had no relationship with the factory. Furthermore, the account statements submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau had many flaws. It was also discovered that the scrap materials were sold for 26,621 yuan, while only 17,717 yuan was distributed to colleagues, leaving a remainder of more than 8,900 yuan embezzled. There was also a revenue of 1,000 yuan for managing flower bags, while only 700 yuan was paid out. The amount was also inconsistent with the second account book submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau, amounting to more than 3,290 yuan in six items. In summary, the embezzlement is factual. Judge Xiao Xiefen asked what evidence they had to support the embezzlement stated in the additional statement of reasons. The plaintiffs gave detailed explanations, but there were too many items to calculate and provide evidence for at once. The plaintiffs' lawyers Gu Hongbiao and You Zhi stated that they requested the court to postpone the case temporarily so that the lawyers could list the reasons and evidence for each item of embezzlement and submit them to the court for review to facilitate the hearing. The court granted the request.

Japanese Ships in China Plan to Make a Comeback 185

Planning to Restore Shipping on Rivers and Sea

Double Tax on Dalian Expected to Be Resolved

Since the September 18th Incident, Japanese ships in China have been hit by the boycott, and dozens of them have stopped operating. However, in areas inhabited by Japanese expatriates, one or two ships still operate empty, as a means of transportation for Japanese people and their activities between countries. Recently, Japanese people have realized that the anti-Japanese sentiment in our country is gradually easing, and their plan to revive shipping has been proceeding at every opportunity. The current active resumption of Japanese ships in China is described in detail below for the reference of those who are concerned about boycotting Japanese goods.

Yangtze River 186

There were originally twenty Japanese ships on the Yangtze River, operating on various ports up and down the Yangtze River. They successively stopped operating in mid-October. Only one Xinyang Maru was left on the upper reaches of the river, and four ships including Yueyang and Nanyang were left on the lower reaches. After the Ruiyang accident, the number of operating ships was reduced to three. For the past four months, all ships have been operating empty, resulting in huge losses. Recently, taking advantage of the fact that anti-Japanese sentiment is not as strong as it was in the previous months, the Japanese began to plan a comeback. They reduced the freight rates for import and export goods between Shanghai and Hankou by 50% across the board, based on the lowest actual amount received. At the same time, they also reduced the fare for passengers traveling up and down the river to Wuhu, Jiujiang, Hankou, and other ports by half. With the secret cooperation of Japanese customs brokers, export goods have suddenly increased as cargo ships and passengers take advantage of the lower prices. Each trip is now crowded with third-class passengers. The Japanese ships that used to travel empty are now suddenly full of cargo and passengers.

Sino-Japanese Route 187

The Sino-Japanese route of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK) in this city has a total of four routes, with nine ships operating. This route has always had the best business due to its monopoly. Each month, the passenger ticket revenue alone averages 90,000 to 100,000 yuan. After September, the business was hit by the boycott, and the number of ships was also reduced. In October and November, revenue plummeted due to Chinese people refusing to board their ships, dropping to only 12,000 to 13,000 yuan per month, a decrease of 80% compared to normal times. The NYK planned to further reduce the number of ships to maintain operations. However, starting in December, sales of third-class tickets for passengers traveling from Shanghai to Japan suddenly increased, and operating revenue also suddenly increased. Last month, it increased from more than 10,000 yuan to about 40,000 yuan. The amount of Japanese goods transported has also gradually increased recently, including tung oil and bran.

Dalian 188

Dalian Bay has always been a free port with no import tax. Since our country agreed last year that foreign goods imported and transferred to Dalian Bay would be subject to an additional 10% import tax, the Japanese have refused to recognize it. As a result, most of the foreign goods transported to South Manchuria were reloaded at Yingkou, Andong, and other ports to avoid paying the double tax. Dalian's import trade has plummeted as a result. The Japanese have been resisting for a year. Until the end of December, the South Manchuria Railway (SMR) authorities and the Dalian Customs authorities negotiated that if the double tax was not recognized, not only would the Dalian port be affected by its decline, but also the SMR's transportation business would suffer a great loss. The development of Yingkou, Andong and other ports caused them to decide that the Dalian Customs would actually recognize our country's double import tax so that foreign goods reported at the Jianghai Customs could still be transferred directly to Dalian. However, the procedures for recognizing this tax have been telegraphed to Shanghai to consult with the Director-General of Customs, and it is said that a certificate will be used as a mark, which is under negotiation.

Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday Morning and Afternoon to Organize Proposals

Outline of Key Points 192

After six hours of careful discussion, each clause was revised, and then it was passed in succession at the first formal meeting held on the afternoon of the same day. Furthermore, the Guangxi representative also arrived in Shanghai on the same day. Currently, there are representatives from as many as sixteen districts, representing four-fifths of all workers. The representatives from each district are full of energy and discuss union affairs for more than twelve hours each day. The future of the conference is very promising, which is probably what our colleagues from afar are pleased to hear. The important points of the general union outline that were passed yesterday (12th) are as follows: ㈠ It is named the National Postal Workers' General Union of the Republic of China. ㈡ The headquarters will be temporarily located in Shanghai. ㈢ The executive committee will consist of eleven members and three alternates, and the supervisory committee will consist of seven members and two alternates. ㈣ Members will pay dues to the general union at a rate of two per thousand of their monthly salary."

The details of each situation are recorded below:

Page 16 194

City Government Measures 195

After the Japanese yarn factories such as the Nichi-Ka, Tongxing, and Xihe factories abolished the monthly bonus, strikes and slowdowns occurred. Party and Government Consultation 196

Workers' Congress 197

The Shanghai West Yarn Factory Workers' Union held a congress of representatives of workers from various Japanese yarn factories at Chunzi Bay, Zhabei, at 9 a.m. yesterday to discuss the Japanese Yarn Factory Association's decision to abolish the monthly bonus. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m.

Representatives Petition 198

Regarding the Japanese yarn factories' abolition of the monthly bonus, the Shanghai West Yarn Factory Workers' Union sent representatives Jiang Yaozong, Li Yugeng, Zhang Wuyun, and Zhou Zhongyi to the City Social Affairs Bureau at 3 a.m. to petition, demanding that negotiations be conducted as soon as possible to restore the monthly bonus in all Japanese yarn factories in the city. The National Medical Association convened its Second Representative Congress in Hangzhou on New Year's Day. The executive committee convened its first meeting of the second session yesterday to discuss various matters: (1) Mutual election of standing committee members: As a result, Xu Naili, Cai Yumen, and Pang Jingzhou were elected. Xu Naili was elected as the standing chairman. Niu Huisheng was then elected as the economic committee member, Wang Qizhang and Jiang Genxun as the documentation committee members, and Yu Yunxiu, Xia Shenchu, and Zhu Qiluo as the editorial committee members. (2) The congress instructed the association to promote the establishment of a pharmaceutical and equipment manufacturing factory. It was resolved to appoint Chu Minyi, Yu Yunxiu, Wang Qizhang, Zhang Zizou, Sheng Peicong, Hua Jitsun, Cheng Muyuan, Wang Wanbai, and Xie Yunshou as special committee members. The first meeting will be convened by the standing committee on January 24th at 5:00 PM. (3) The congress instructed the organization of a pathological anatomy voluntary association. It was resolved that all those who sympathize with the cause, whether members of the association or not, are free to join, and Yu Yunxiu, Pang Jingzhou, You Pengxi, and Wu Yichu were appointed to draft the plan for further solicitation of cooperation from comrades. (4) Promoting medical and pharmaceutical education to safeguard the foundation of the nation: It was resolved to appoint Pang Jingzhou, Wang Qizhang, Cai Yumen, Guo Qiyuan, and Yan Fuqing to review and implement the plan. (5) Training midwives and improving traditional birth attendants to value human life, and banning unqualified midwives to respect humanity: It was resolved to follow the congress's resolution and urge the health authorities to strictly enforce the "Ten Regulations for Midwives" and the "Rules for Managing Traditional Birth Attendants." (6) Establishing a medical construction committee to formulate a national medical implementation outline with a unified goal and defined procedures: It was resolved to first ask Xia Shenchu to draft the outline and then submit it for discussion. (7) Proposing to the central government that medical and health personnel should be elected as members of the Legislative Yuan: It was resolved to ask the Nanjing Medical Association to conduct a survey nearby. (8) Proposing that the Ministry of Interior's Health Department forward a request to the Ministry of Justice to expedite the enactment of special regulations to protect forensic doctors for nationwide court compliance: It was resolved to proceed as requested. (9) Submitting a request to the government to expedite the reorganization of military hygiene, replenish medical and health personnel to increase the military's combat power against Japan, and establish a committee for soliciting medical and health personnel for combat against Japan: It was resolved to proceed as requested. (10) Prescriptions should not use secret formulas: It was resolved to notify all doctors nationwide in the name of the association that secret formulas should not be used from now on. Violators will be warned by the association for the first offense. If pharmacies receive secret formulas, they should report them to the medical and pharmaceutical association for disposal. However, hospital formulations prepared within the hospital are not subject to this restriction. (11) Submitting a request to the central government to determine local health administrative funding: It was resolved to merge it with the 56th proposal for reference. (12) Promoting the cultivation of raw medicinal materials. (13) Doctors nationwide should urge or support the development of new domestic drug manufacturing to expedite the implementation of anti-Japanese work. It was resolved that these two proposals be combined with the first proposal for reference by the special committee.

Shutdown Tide at Italian Dye Factory 201

Police Interference Causes Misunderstanding

The Factory Files Lawsuit with the Court

After the Italian silk dyeing factory on Jin Shenfu Road announced its closure, all the workers demanded its reopening. The Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau are working to mediate. The factory reported the interference of the police the other day, which caused panic among the workers. The situation at that time was quite serious. The details of the situation are recorded separately as follows:

Police Interference with the Italian Dye Factory: Due to business reasons, after being forced to announce its closure on December 21st, the Dyeing Industry Union Silk Office and the factory manager Kong Rongqing reported to the party and government authorities for handling. The factory was deeply afraid that the workers would cause trouble at the factory, so they reported to the French police to maintain order. The Lujiawan police sent a large number of armed detectives, which caused great panic among the workers and a slight misunderstanding.

Party and Government Advise: Xu Yefu, Deputy Section Chief of the Civil Affairs Section of the Municipal Party Department, dispatched staff member Wu Jiaze. Mai Chaoshu, Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, dispatched staff member Qiu Peihao to jointly explain everything to the political department of the French police and requested the withdrawal of the detectives to avoid conflict. The police department completely withdrew the armed detectives in the afternoon. At the same time, the party and government authorities tried to mediate.

Filing a Lawsuit: Kong Rongqing, manager of the Italian Dye Factory, stated that the factory's actions in dealing with the workers this time were out of necessity, not intentionally to dismiss the workers, but the workers did not forgive them and disputes arose. Yesterday, he officially appointed lawyer Bian Jialu to file a lawsuit with the court, demanding compensation from the workers for the losses. This document has been submitted to the court by lawyer Bian Jialu. In addition, the Italian Dye Factory on Xinglong Street and the wholesale office on Gongguanju Road have also stopped operating since yesterday. The factory has requested the French police to send detectives to protect them.

Union Resolutions: The Silk Office of the Dyeing Industry Occupational Union, due to the Italian factory's expulsion of workers and the expansion of the dispute, held a joint meeting of representatives from various factories. Chairman Jin Tai reported on the resolutions of the various cases: 1. How to assist the workers who are being oppressed by force by the Italian factory? It was resolved to unanimously resist to the end and vow not to yield in order to achieve the goal of resuming work. 2. How to deal with the Italian factory owner's expulsion of workers? It was resolved that: (1) Report to the party and government authorities for strict handling and request immediate resumption of work. (2) Each factory will send one representative to question the co-industry association Zhu Wenqi. 3. It was resolved to report Zhang Aida's case of concealment to the authorities for punishment. 4. Omitted. 5. Whether to organize a special committee to handle the Italian dispute for discussion. It was resolved to appoint Ren Xinglin and other nine people to immediately organize a special committee to handle the Italian incident.

Three Municipal Committee Members Request Removal of Land Section Chief Wang Shuzhen 203

Yang Xinzheng, Municipal Committee Member of Caohejing, Chen Ya夫, Municipal Committee Member of Pusong District, and Yang Hongjun, Municipal Committee Member of Fahua District, etc., requested Director Jin yesterday to remove the current Wang Shuzhen, Chief of the Fourth Section of the Land Bureau, as soon as possible to appease public anger, because Wang Shuzhen's handling of affairs is perverse and disregards the people's sentiments. The document stated, "Wang Shuzhen, Chief of the Fourth Section, is self-willed and obstinate, and he gained his current position by catering to the former Director Zhu. Relying on the exclusive trust, he repeatedly offered policies that abused the people. Local people have long been resentful and have filed numerous complaints, but the former Director Zhu turned a deaf ear. If he was not deliberately protecting him, he was undoubtedly blinded by Chief Wang. Let's take the more prominent examples: For the issuance of land ownership certificates, which is originally intended to consolidate the people's property rights, the responsibility lies in being swift and efficient. However, when people go to the section to exchange them, they often make things difficult in various ways, saying that the grain quota is inconsistent or that the name is incorrect, and they are rejected and not processed, causing landowners to shrink back. Although the land of each household in development has been developed for a long time, only a few have obtained land ownership certificates. In the past, the transfer and analysis of civil real estate often had mismatched grain quotas and names, which were not unusual. What is the intention of the section in not processing them and nitpicking? Furthermore, there are regulations for issuing land ownership certificates, but there are cases of concealment and fraudulent claims. The section does not investigate carefully. Even after the landowners have provided proof of ownership in many ways, they are still not processed. No wonder public opinion is in an uproar, and everyone believes that land ownership certificates are issued to reorganize the land, but now the issuance of land ownership certificates has led to property rights errors and confusion, which is disappointing to the people. When land is transferred, the parties must go to the bureau together to fill out application forms and other procedures. The section's responsibility is to understand the people's sentiments. Just think, can homeowners avoid spending time and money by running back and forth for a small amount of land price? Without Dong Bao and others present to testify, if there is theft of certificates and illegal sales, can we guarantee that there will be no disputes? In the past, the Shanghai County Government had a proposal to abolish official contracts and distribute them to the industry, but local people believed that it was a harsh government and abuse of the people, so they stopped it immediately. This shows the psychology of the people and the way for politicians to follow. Although the method of transferring and registering land certificates has been approved by the mayor, why does the section insist on making things difficult for the people to the point of being a puppet? Even more seriously, the land prices of each land lot have been assessed and reported long ago, but the section arbitrarily increases them when the people pay taxes, causing widespread confusion and public resentment. After hearing and seeing this, the committee members are uneasy to remain silent. We are deeply pleased that the former Director Zhu has already left office, and Your Excellency's arrival is the beginning of a new era. It is time to change course and start anew. We are determined to base our decisions on public opinion, and we dare to present the situation below, requesting that the section chief be removed as soon as possible to appease public anger and assist in rectification. We are extremely urgent."

Reader Correspondence

The Path That Students Should Take in the Future 218

Reading to save the country.

Become one with the peasants and workers.

A spirit of transcendence. A worldly career. Huang Juemin

Students are the pillars of the country and the pioneers of society. The scholar-official class that stood before them was so corrupt, and the countless masses that stood behind them were so ignorant. Therefore, the country's future depends only on these few young students to release a ray of dawn in the long night. At present, internal and external troubles are pressing heavily, and all those with blood and spirit are united against the enemy, especially the youth. There is a need for guidance at the crossroads. Based on my humble opinion, I would like to offer the path that young people should take in the future to my dear young students. Some say that the country's difficulties have reached a critical moment, so how can there be leisurely words? I do not know that the current situation in our country is like a seven-year illness seeking wormwood for three years. First, recently, the views on students saving the country in our country have been inconsistent. Some say that students should study, some say that students should teach the country, and some say that studying should not forget saving the country, and saving the country should not forget studying. I mean that what is said above is not correct. It must be known that reading to save the country is two aspects of the same event and cannot be separated. Reading is the means, and saving the country is the goal. However, this so-called reading is different from reading to death. In the future, our reading is not a replaying of lectures like a phonograph. We should enter society and seek knowledge in society, striving to ensure that the knowledge gained has a close relationship with society and is used in society to obtain greater gains. We believe that today's China has reached a major turning point. If we want to wash away all the old legacy and seek the survival of the masses and find a way out, then we must strive for the struggle to reform the current social organization, and seek the development of new forces in the struggle. Therefore, the first path that students should take in the future is to read to save the country. Second, today's China is not the country of the masses, but the country of bureaucrats and warlords. How can it be expected to pacify the country internally and resist foreign aggression? Only the peasant and worker masses have the ability to resist the oppression of imperialism. Although young students have the will and enthusiasm to resist imperialism, they themselves lack the power. The only way to achieve their wishes is to awaken the peasant and worker masses and become one with the peasants and workers, and establish a great and lasting force to fight imperialism to the death, and to fight to the death with all traitors who lose power and humiliate the country. Therefore, the second path that students should take in the future is to become one with the peasants and workers. Third, the young students under the rampage of the tyrant can be roughly divided into two major groups: one is determined to sacrifice themselves and fight to the death with the enemy; the other is to prolong their lives and endure death to fill this weak China. The former is commendable for their loyalty, but if they die, they will not bear any responsibility. It seems too easy. Strictly speaking, they dare to say that they have exhausted the duties of youth. Youth is the backbone of the nation, and like white blood cells in the human body, if white blood cells are lacking, diseases will take advantage of it. If the backbone dies, the vitality of the nation will also decrease, causing great losses to the nation. Therefore, young people in the future should know that this is not the time to die, but to actively temper their physique, strengthen their will, not fear difficulties, not live in ease, hold the spirit of certain death, and devote themselves to society, devote themselves to humanity, seek welfare for society, and strive for the survival of humanity. Therefore, the third path that students should dare to take in the future is to do a worldly career with a spirit of transcendence. (Yi)

Shanghai Local Edition of Shen Bao, Thursday, January 14, 21st Year of the Republic of China (Free of Charge) Small Forum

The Deformed Development of Shanghai Society 220

— Mian Yi

If we cast our eyes on the general phenomena of Shanghai society today, there is a common morbid state, which is the development of a deformed Shanghai society. In ordinary times, we do not see any special signs, but if we analyze it carefully with a microscope, all the evils in society can be summarized into this deformed development of society, and we can get a definite and irrefutable answer.

We know that no matter what things, there must be equal development in order to gradually seek progress. On the contrary, one thing is a laggard in the times and is degenerating, while at the same time, the same thing is surpassing the times and progressing. This contradictory evolution丨deformed development丨will never have good results, and even to the point of making things so bad that they cannot be cleaned up. Now we take the facts in society to prove:

In the ordinary life of ordinary people in society, no one is satisfied with the current situation and does not want to move towards a more comfortable life. However, the life of the poor still lingers in the hard life of working at sunrise and resting at sunset in ancient times, earning their own food, while at the same time, the rich enjoy the blessed life of hugging charming wives and concubines, living in foreign houses, and riding in cars. This disparity in the lives of the rich and poor is the most obvious phenomenon in society.

The result of this phenomenon is the instability of personal life, because everyone admires and wants to get a more comfortable life than themselves, and is dissatisfied with their current life, so they use various methods to pursue that new comfortable life, and all the evils in society have occurred.

How did this morbidity happen? In simple terms, it is the deformed development of society. The life of various European and American countries is more stable than that of China. They ride in cars, eat big meals, live in foreign houses, dance, decorate, and everything is several times higher than China. This consumption is what Chinese people crave and want to imitate, but what about their production? The era of handicraft industry is over, and the iron industry has reached the last scene with the prelude of the times. Due to the development of science, it has progressed to the mechanical electrical industry. At the same time, our Chinese production is still the handicraft industry of the eighteenth century, and has not yet entered the iron industry of the nineteenth century, let alone the electrical industry of the twentieth century.

Now we can know that the stability of social life in European and American countries is due to the parallel development of production and consumption. The instability of social life in China is due to the deformed development. We only learn the consumption of the twentieth century, but not the production of the twentieth century. How can society not show the precarious instability?

Popular Literature

A Scene of Indignation 221

This scene of indignation took place at the Paotaiwan Railway Station.

It was around nine o'clock in the morning, not long after the train had departed, when three or four children scavenging for coal cinders desperately scrambled for the freshly scattered embers in the tracks. Several rickshaws were parked humorously beside the rails, the drivers squatting in front of their vehicles, puffing away at their paper cigarettes.

Several long benches lay scattered about the station, where one or two workers sat idly. In one corner sat a young man dressed in a police uniform, reading the day's newspaper with a stern expression, as if paying attention to a very important piece of news.

He was a student at the Railway Police Training Institute, named Chen Yuming, a young man with a fervent spirit.

Suddenly, as if struck by a significant stimulus, he leaped up, his deeply set eyes emitting a fierce light. The veins on his square forehead pulsed. He let out a howl, "Ah!" and then sat back down, resuming his search in the newspaper.

One or two of the workers glanced at him unconsciously, then continued sitting idly.

He leaped up a second time and frantically tore the newspapers into pieces, making a "Whish! Whish! Whish!" sound. In an instant, the ground, five square feet in size, was covered with dry, brittle scraps of paper.

The children scavenging for coal cinders also stood up, murmuring in soft northern accents to each other. The workers glanced at him again for a moment.

Chen Yuming was a sanguine young man. After Japan forcibly occupied the Northeast, a violent fury surged within him. A crimson flame burned in his heart, and an alarm bell clanged wildly in his mind.

Suddenly, he roared again, as if mad:

"We're doomed! My country!"

He was like a wild horse that had lost its reins, a giant beast that had escaped its cage! He rushed madly into the kitchen of the Railway Police Training Institute, and cruelly and swiftly, he took a gleaming kitchen knife and severed half of the middle finger on his left hand. Blood flowed like an opened faucet, drenching the ground and soaking his clothes.

Thus, the tragic scene came to a close. Chen Yuming lay on the ground, unconscious.

The next day, a certain newspaper carried this news item:

"Chen Yuming, a student at the Railway Training Institute, from Beiping, Hebei, 23 years old, suddenly went to the kitchen yesterday morning around 9:00 a.m., took a kitchen knife, and severed half of the middle finger on his left hand. Blood poured out, and he fainted instantly. It is said that the student is usually very concerned about national affairs and has repeatedly considered joining the army to serve in the Northeast, but gave up due to lack of opportunity. He acted out of indignation. The institute sent the student to the Haibin Hospital for treatment."

Popular Science

Home First-Aid for Small Fires 222

— Tao Xiaotao

We must always be particularly careful with fire, whether at home, at school, or anywhere else. If we are not careful, we could burn things, or worse, burn down houses and kill people. How terrifying that would be!

When we are sleeping, do not leave candles or kerosene lamps lit by the bed, to avoid accidental danger. We must always be attentive when cooking or burning anything in the house. Do not discard used cigarette butts in vehicles or on the floor. Keep flammable materials to a minimum in the house. Do not let sparks fall on the floor when cooking. These are all things we should know and pay attention to every day. Don't think that dropping a cigarette butt on the floor or having a few things in the house doesn't matter. The recent fire on the Datong Steamer, which killed more than two hundred people, was caused by a cigarette butt.

Now, I will write down how to put out a fire:

When a house catches fire, close all the windows in the house to cut off the air supply and quickly remove flammable materials. This will make it easier to put out the fire, as the air supplies oxygen that fuels the flames. Oxygen can make the fire burn bigger and bigger. Then, observing which side the fire is on, pour a large amount of water from the roof, and the fire will be extinguished easily. Some people panic when their clothes catch fire and try to take them off quickly. But before the clothes can be removed, the fire has already burned the flesh. Some people are even burned to death. When your clothes catch fire, you must immediately lie down on the ground and roll around. The flames will not get oxygen to fuel them, and they will be extinguished. This is a very good method.

If the mosquito net on your bed catches fire, you must quickly press the bedding tightly on the burning part of the net. The fire will not get oxygen to fuel it, and it will be extinguished. Although you sacrifice a bed of blankets, it saves the house and the people inside, which is worthwhile.

These are simple methods for putting out small fires. While fighting the fire, you must also quickly call the fire brigade to prevent the fire from growing bigger and beyond control.

East, West, South, North

King of Authors: H.G. Wells 223

"Science is valuable, but if it cannot be used by the people, it is of no benefit to mankind. The value of learning is certainly great, but if it does not become something the masses can use, it has no great value."

These two thoughts were the driving force behind H.G. Wells, the British authority on literary thought, to completely change direction and become a novelist of idealism. To realize this belief, he devoted himself to writing without rest. This was not just for five or ten years, but continued until his sixty-fourth year, and will continue until he dies. Ah! Great faith and great effort!

He has completed more than a hundred works. Novels, commentaries, histories—he is truly skilled in every genre. But since the publication of his debut work, "Select Conversations with an Uncle," in 1895, especially after the publication of "The Outline of History" in 1920, he has written from a position of peaceful idealism, which undoubtedly marked a new era in the world of modern writing. "The Outline of History" has been translated into various languages and is popular all over the world. He is truly worthy of being called a king of authors.

Street Sociology

Various Ways of Life (2) Xingzi 224

I have encountered such things several times, but I cannot tell whether they are comedies or tragedies.

○ ○ ○ ○

Once, the protagonist of this comedy or tragedy was an old man with white hair. He was carrying a wonton noodle stand, wandering around Jing'an Temple. At that time, Jing'an Temple was holding a temple fair, and the ladies seeking blessings, wealth, longevity, and children were extremely crowded. Naturally, this was an excellent time to give alms and accumulate merit.

I watched as the old man carried his wonton noodle stand, jostling through the crowd, his trembling hands knocking on the bamboo clapper at one end of the stand, making a sorrowful "cry." Suddenly, the old man and his stand fell together. Both the stand and the old man cried out in pain. The bowls were smashed, and the wontons fell to the ground. Then, the old man began to wail loudly, picking up a banana peel from the ground.

"This stand is my lifeblood! Damn it, these useless feet! They had to step on this banana peel! All my capital is gone! What am I going to do? Heaven, my bitter fate..."

As he cried, he lamented. Old tears streamed down, dripping little by little onto the dust. The broken bowls and scattered wontons on the ground seemed to let out heavy sighs. "People" are, after all, cooperative and sympathetic creatures, and this was the best time to give alms and accumulate merit. The sorrowful cries touched the hearts of the pious men and women, and so one or two coins were thrown into the old man's hand, because they knew that it was not only saving this poor old life but also accumulating "good for good" blessings for themselves.

The old man, facing this group of charitable men and women, repeatedly thanked them while gathering up the scattered wonton stand. In his tearful eyes, a triumphant smile was revealed.

○ ○ ○ ○

The other incidents were exactly the same, but with different protagonists. Some people say that this is a trick to get money. Shanghai is a world full of wonders. However, I think, is it not a tragedy that an old man with white hair relies on this trick to eke out a living?

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (8) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 225

X The Conflict Between British and American Consuls

The British were the first to establish a concession in Shanghai. Naturally, they wanted to monopolize the concession, especially the British Consul, Balfour, who was adamant and did not allow the people of any other country to set foot in the concession.

After the signing of the Sino-American and Sino-French trade treaties, merchants from the United States and France cited the most-favored-nation clause and demanded that merchants from both countries enjoy the same rights as the British in the concession. This led to a conflict within the concession among the imperialists themselves.

The first U.S. Consul stationed in Shanghai, Wolcott (H.G.Wo;cptt), first established a consulate in the concession and raised the American flag. The British Consul and the Daotai of Songjiang and Taicang opposed this, arguing that only the British flag could be flown within the concession. However, U.S. Consul Wolcott insisted on his position. As a result, he was allowed to fly the American flag. At that time, the British Consulate in Shanghai was still located in the city and had not yet moved into the concession. Only the American flag was flying in the concession. When British Consul Balfour opposed the American flag being raised, the Governor of Hong Kong did not think so. In a telegram from the Governor of Hong Kong to Balfour, he said: "It is doubtful whether British officials have the right to interfere with the raising of a flag by officials from other countries." It can be seen that the reason why the British Consul in Shanghai did not have a major conflict with the American Consul this time was entirely because the Governor of Hong Kong did not agree with Balfour's position.

Reply 226

To Mr. Jiang Xiaoguang: This publication has now changed its style. Previous book and newspaper introductions, women's life...everything that is natural has been deleted. We appreciate your suggestion to allocate a corner of space for readers to discuss literature and art. However, the space is too small to maneuver. We will discuss it again when the space is expanded.

Regulations for Soliciting Articles for the Local Supplement 227

(1) All kinds of miscellaneous articles about literature, art, and society, such as (1) poems and short articles related to current affairs, (2) miscellaneous articles that improve, criticize, or satirize society.

(1) In addition to the above two types, this publication also welcomes other miscellaneous articles that are extremely interesting and valuable. However, please note that all articles should be related to Shanghai facts.

(1) Brevity is the soul of wit. Articles should be about 400 to 500 words long and should not exceed 800 words at most.

(1) Manuscripts must be written directly, with legible characters. Do not use foreign paper or write on both sides. Western script should be used sparingly.

(1) The manuscript must be stamped so that it can be checked later when collecting the remuneration.

(1) The envelope of the submission should clearly state "Editorial Department of the Local Supplement" to receive the mail.

(1) All submissions will not be returned, whether they are published or not. If a return is required, please declare it in advance and attach a postage stamp of one or four cents.

(1) The remuneration for articles is divided into three grades: A, B, and C. Grade A is four yuan, Grade B is three yuan, and Grade C is two yuan. Special articles will be compensated separately.
